                <p class="notranslate">
                  This section introduces simple windows and GUI controls in Java. It is mostly

                    &hellip;
                    <a href="#"><i class="fa fa-caret-down"></i></a>
                </p>
              </div>

              <p class="j-desc-expand description description-expanded notranslate" itemprop="description">
                This section introduces simple windows and GUI controls in Java. It is mostly
<br />a precursor to the later sections on Swing, so you can move there gradually by
<br />learning some of the basic concepts before diving into the larger and more
<br />complex (but better!) library. See http:&#x2F;&#x2F;courses.coreservlets.com&#x2F;Course-Materials&#x2F;java.html for the full tutorial, associated code, exercises, and exercise solutions. You can also download PDF files of each lecture, for saving or printing. Please email hall@coreservlets.com for info on how to arrange customized courses on Java 7, Java 8, JSF 2.2, PrimeFaces, Hadoop, and other Java EE topics onsite at YOUR location.

GUI Libraries
in Java SE

  <li itemprop="text">

        5.
      </a>
    GUI Libraries in Java
Part of Java SE
&#x2022; AWT (Abstract Window Toolkit)
&#x2013; The original GUI library in Java
1.02. Native Look and Feel (LAF).
&#x2022; Covered in this lecture
&#x2013; Purposes
&#x2022; Easy building of simple-looking
interfaces
&#x2013; Often for internal purposes
only. Not seen by end users.
&#x2022; First step toward learning
Swing
&#x2022; Swing
&#x2013; GUI library added to Java starting
in Java 1.1
&#x2022; Covered in later lectures
&#x2013; Purposes
&#x2022; Professional looking GUIs that
follow standard
&#x2022; GUIs with the same look and
feel on multiple platforms
Extensions
&#x2022; SWT (Standard Widget Toolkit)
&#x2013; GUI from the Eclipse foundation.
Native LAF ala AWT.
&#x2022; See http://www.eclipse.org/swt/
&#x2013; Purposes
&#x2022; Higher-performance professional
looking GUIs
&#x2022; Native LAF
&#x2022; Interaction with the Eclipse Rich
Client Platform
&#x2022; Java FX
&#x2013; GUI library and tools now
standardized separately
&#x2022; See http://javafx.com/
&#x2022; Part of Java SE starting in Java 8
&#x2013; Purposes
&#x2022; XML-based layout
&#x2022; Mobile platforms
&#x2022; Rich media: audio, video, etc.
7

Background

  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-7-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 7 image" target="_blank">
        7.
      </a>
    Windows and Layout
Management
&#x2022; Containers
&#x2013; Most windows are a Container that can hold other
windows or GUI components. Canvas is the major
exception.
&#x2022; Layout Managers
&#x2013; Containers have a LayoutManager that automatically
sizes and positions components that are in the window
&#x2013; You can change the behavior of the layout manager or
disable it completely. Details in next lecture.
&#x2022; Events
&#x2013; Windows and components can receive mouse and
keyboard events, just as in previous lecture.
9
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-8-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 8 image" target="_blank">
        8.
      </a>
    Windows and Layout
Management (Continued)
&#x2022; Drawing in Windows
&#x2013; To draw into a window, make a subclass with its own
paint method
&#x2013; Having one window draw into another window is not
usually recommended
&#x2022; Popup Windows
&#x2013; Some windows (Frame and Dialog) have their own
title bar and border and can be placed at arbitrary
locations on the screen
&#x2013; Other windows (Canvas an Panel) are embedded into
existing windows only
10
 
  </li>

Customized Java EE Training: http://courses.coreservlets.com/

Foundational AWT
Window Types
11
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-10-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 10 image" target="_blank">
        10.
      </a>
    Summary
&#x2022; Canvas
&#x2013; Purpose:
&#x2022; Reusable picture or drawing area. Basis for custom component.
&#x2013; Code
&#x2022; Allocate Canvas, give it a size, add it to existing window.
&#x2022; Panel
&#x2013; Purpose
&#x2022; To group other components into rectangular regions.
&#x2013; Code
&#x2022; Allocate Panel, put other components in it, add to window.
&#x2022; Frame
&#x2013; Purpose
&#x2022; Core popup window. Main window for your application.
&#x2013; Code
&#x2022; Allocate Frame, give it a size, add stuff to it, pop it up.
12
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-11-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 11 image" target="_blank">
        11.
      </a>
    Canvas
&#x2022; Major purposes
&#x2013; A drawing area
&#x2013; A custom component that does not need to contain any
other component (e.g., an image button)
&#x2022; Default layout manager: none
&#x2013; Canvas is not a Container, so cannot enclose components
&#x2022; Creating and using
&#x2013; Allocate it
&#x2022; Canvas c = new Canvas();
&#x2013; Give it a size
&#x2022; c.setSize(width, height);
&#x2013; Drop it in existing window
&#x2022; someWindow.add(c);13
Since Canvas is often the starting point for a component that has
a custom paint method or event handlers, you often do
MySpecializedCanvas c = new MySpecializedCanvas(&#x2026;).
If this code is in the main window, then &#x201C;someWindow&#x201D; is &#x201C;this&#x201D; and can be omitted.
I.e, the init method of an applet would add a Canvas to itself just with &#x201C;add(c);&#x201D;.
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-12-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 12 image" target="_blank">
        12.
      </a>
    Canvas Example
import java.awt.*;
/** A Circle component built using a Canvas. */
public class Circle extends Canvas {
private int width, height;
public Circle(Color foreground, int radius) {
setForeground(foreground);
width = 2*radius;
height = 2*radius;
setSize(width, height);
}
public void paint(Graphics g) {
g.fillOval(0, 0, width, height);
}
public void setCenter(int x, int y) {
setLocation(x - width/2, y - height/2);
}
}14
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-13-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 13 image" target="_blank">
        13.
      </a>
    Canvas Example (Continued)
import java.awt.*;
import java.applet.Applet;
public class CircleTest extends Applet {
public void init() {
setBackground(Color.LIGHT_GRAY);
add(new Circle(Color.WHITE, 30));
add(new Circle(Color.GRAY, 40));
add(new Circle(Color.BLACK, 50));
}
}

  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-14-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 14 image" target="_blank">
        14.

    Canvases are Rectangular and
Opaque: Example
public class CircleTest2 extends Applet {
public void init() {
setBackground(Color.LIGHT_GRAY);
setLayout(null); // Turn off layout manager.
Circle circle;
int radius = getSize().width/6;
int deltaX = round(2.0 * (double)radius / Math.sqrt(2.0));
for (int x=radius; x&lt;6*radius; x=x+deltaX) {
circle = new Circle(Color.BLACK, radius);
add(circle);
circle.setCenter(x, x);
}
}
private int round(double num) {
return((int)Math.round(num));
}
}
16
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-15-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 15 image" target="_blank">
        15.
      </a>
    Lightweight Components
&#x2022; Idea
&#x2013; Regular AWT windows are native windows behind the
scenes. So, they are rectangular and opaque.
&#x2013; You can make &#x201C;lightweight components&#x201D; &#x2013; components
that are really pictures, not windows, behind the scenes.
&#x2022; These don&#x2019;t have the rectangular/opaque restrictions, but
building them is usually more trouble than it is worth in the
AWT library. The Swing library makes it simple with a
&#x201C;setOpaque&#x201D; method.
&#x2022; Code
&#x2013; If you really want to do it yourself in AWT, you have to
tell Java how to calculate the minimum and preferred
sizes (see later section on layout managers).
&#x2022; Even so, it can have tricky interactions if the enclosing
window has a custom paint method. Use Swing instead!
17
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-16-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 16 image" target="_blank">
        16.
      </a>
    Lightweight Components:
Example
public class BetterCircle extends Component {
private Dimension preferredDimension;
private int width, height;
public BetterCircle(Color foreground, int radius) {
setForeground(foreground);
width = 2*radius; height = 2*radius;
preferredDimension = new Dimension(width, height);
setSize(preferredDimension);
}
public void paint(Graphics g) {
g.setColor(getForeground());
g.fillOval(0, 0, width, height);
}
public Dimension getPreferredSize() {
return(preferredDimension);
}
public Dimension getMinimumSize() {
return(preferredDimension);
}
...18
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-17-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 17 image" target="_blank">
        17.
      </a>
    Component Class
&#x2022; Idea
&#x2013; Ancestor of all graphical components in Java (even
Swing). So, methods here are shared by all windows and
controls.
&#x2022; Useful methods
&#x2013; getBackground/setBackground
&#x2013; getForeground/setForeground
&#x2022; Change/lookup the default foreground color
&#x2022; Color is inherited by the Graphics object of the component
&#x2013; getFont/setFont
&#x2022; Returns/sets the current font
&#x2022; Inherited by the Graphics object of the component
&#x2013; paint
&#x2022; Called whenever the user call repaint or when the
component is obscured and reexposed
19
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-18-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 18 image" target="_blank">
        18.
      </a>
    Component Class (Continued)
&#x2022; Useful methods
&#x2013; setVisible
&#x2022; Exposes (true) or hides (false) the component
&#x2022; Especially useful for frames and dialogs
&#x2013; setSize/setBounds/setLocation
&#x2013; getSize/getBounds/getLocation
&#x2022; Physical aspects (size and position) of the component
&#x2013; list
&#x2022; Prints out info on this component and any components it
contains; useful for debugging
&#x2013; invalidate/validate
&#x2022; Tell layout manager to redo the layout
&#x2013; getParent
&#x2022; Returns enclosing window (or null if there is none)20
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-19-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 19 image" target="_blank">
        19.
      </a>
    Panel
&#x2022; Major purposes
&#x2013; To group/organize components
&#x2013; A custom component that requires embedded components
&#x2022; Default layout manager: FlowLayout
&#x2013; Shrinks components to their preferred (minimum) size
&#x2013; Places them left to right in centered rows
&#x2022; Creating and using
&#x2013; Allocate it
&#x2022; Panel p = new Panel();
&#x2013; Put stuff into it
&#x2022; p.add(someButton);
&#x2022; p.add(someOtherWidget);
&#x2013; Drop the Panel in an existing window
&#x2022; someWindow.add(p);21
Note the lack of an explicit setSize. The size of a Panel is
usually determined by a combination of what the Panel
contains and the layout manager of the window that
contains the Panel.
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-20-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 20 image" target="_blank">
        20.
      </a>
    No Panels: Example
import java.applet.Applet;
import java.awt.*;
public class ButtonTest1 extends Applet {
public void init() {
String[] labelPrefixes = { "Start", "Stop", "Pause",
"Resume" };
for (int i=0; i&lt;4; i++) {
add(new Button(labelPrefixes[i] + " Thread1"));
}
for (int i=0; i&lt;4; i++) {
add(new Button(labelPrefixes[i] + " Thread2"));
}
}
}

    No Panels: Result

    Panels: Example
import java.applet.Applet;
import java.awt.*;
public class ButtonTest2 extends Applet {
public void init() {
String[] labelPrefixes = { "Start", "Stop", "Pause",
"Resume" };
Panel p1 = new Panel();
for (int i=0; i&lt;4; i++) {
p1.add(new Button(labelPrefixes[i] + " Thread1"));
}
Panel p2 = new Panel();
for (int i=0; i&lt;4; i++) {
p2.add(new Button(labelPrefixes[i] + " Thread2"));
}
add(p1);
add(p2);
}
}

  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-23-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 23 image" target="_blank">
        23.

    Panels: Result
25
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-24-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 24 image" target="_blank">
        24.
      </a>
    Container Class
&#x2022; Idea
&#x2013; Ancestor of all window types except Canvas. So, these methods are
common among almost all windows.
&#x2022; Useful Container methods
&#x2013; add
&#x2022; Add a component to the container (in the last position in the
component array)
&#x2022; If using BorderLayout, you can also specify in which region to
place the component
&#x2013; remove
&#x2022; Remove the component from the window (container)
&#x2013; getComponents
&#x2022; Returns an array of components in the window
&#x2022; Used by layout managers
&#x2013; setLayout
&#x2022; Changes the layout manager associated with the window26
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-25-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 25 image" target="_blank">
        25.
      </a>
    Frame Class
&#x2022; Major Purpose
&#x2013; A stand-alone window with its own title and menu bar,
border, cursor, and icon image
&#x2022; Can contain other GUI components
&#x2022; Default layout manager: BorderLayout
&#x2013; BorderLayout
&#x2022; Divides the screen into 5 regions: North, South, East,
West, and Center
&#x2013; To switch to the applet&#x2019;s layout manager use
&#x2022; setLayout(new FlowLayout());
&#x2022; Creating and using &#x2013; two approaches:
&#x2013; A fixed-size Frame
&#x2013; A Frame that stretches to fit what it contains
27
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-26-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 26 image" target="_blank">
        26.
      </a>
    Creating a Fixed-Size Frame
&#x2022; Approach
Frame frame = new Frame(titleString);
frame.add(somePanel, BorderLayout.CENTER);
frame.add(otherPanel, BorderLayout.NORTH);
...
frame.setSize(width, height);
frame.setVisible(true);
&#x2022; Note: be sure you pop up the frame last
&#x2013; Odd behavior results if you add components to a window
that is already visible (unless you call doLayout on the
frame)
28
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-27-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 27 image" target="_blank">
        27.
      </a>
    Creating a Frame that Stretches
to Fit What it Contains
&#x2022; Approach
Frame frame = new Frame(titleString);
frame.setLocation(left, top);
frame.add(somePanel, BorderLayout.CENTER);
...
frame.pack();
frame.setVisible(true);
&#x2022; Note
&#x2013; Again, be sure to pop up the frame after adding the
components
29
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-28-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 28 image" target="_blank">
        28.
      </a>
    Frame Example 1
&#x2022; Creating the Frame object in main
public class FrameExample1 {
public static void main(String[] args) {
Frame f = new Frame("Frame Example 1");
f.setSize(400, 300);
f.setVisible(true);
}
}

&#x2022; Using a Subclass of Frame
public class FrameExample2 extends Frame {
public FrameExample2() {

setSize(400, 300);
setVisible(true);
}
public static void main(String[] args) {
new FrameExample2();
}

31
The &#x201C;main&#x201D; method that instantiates the Frame need not reside in
FrameExample2. The idea is that you make a reusable Frame
class, and then that class can be popped up various different
ways (from main, when the user clicks a button, when certain
events occur in your app, etc.)
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-30-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 30 image" target="_blank">
        30.
      </a>
    A Closeable Frame
&#x2022; CloseableFrame.java
public class CloseableFrame extends Frame {
public CloseableFrame(String title) {
super(title);
addWindowListener(new ExitListener());
}
}
&#x2022; ExitListener.java
public class ExitListener extends WindowAdapter {
public void windowClosing(WindowEvent event) {
System.exit(0);
}
}
32
Download these two classes from the source code in the tutorial,
then use CloseableFrame wherever you would have used Frame.

AWT GUI Controls and
Event Processing
34
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-33-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 33 image" target="_blank">
        33.
      </a>
    AWT GUI Controls
&#x2022; Characteristics (vs. windows)
&#x2013; Automatically drawn &#x2013; you don&#x2019;t override paint
&#x2013; Positioned by layout manager
&#x2013; Use native window-system controls (widgets)
&#x2022; Controls adopt look and feel of underlying window system
&#x2013; Higher level events typically used
&#x2022; For example, for buttons you don&#x2019;t monitor mouse clicks,
since most OS&#x2019;s also let you trigger a button by hitting
RETURN when the button has the keyboard focus
35
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-34-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 34 image" target="_blank">
        34.
      </a>
    GUI Event Processing
Strategies
&#x2022; Decentralized event processing
&#x2013; Component (e.g., Button) has its own event handler
&#x2022; Harder to call methods in the main app, so works best
when operations are relatively independent
&#x2022; Centralized event processing
&#x2013; Have main app implement listener. Send all events there.
&#x2022; Easier for handler to call methods from the main app
&#x2022; But, if you have multiple buttons, you will need if/then/else
in the event-handler method
&#x2022; Semi-centralized event processing
&#x2013; Use inner class for event handling
&#x2022; Better than interface if you have many different buttons
36
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-35-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 35 image" target="_blank">
        35.
      </a>
    Decentralized Event Processing:
Example
import java.awt.*;
public class ActionExample1 extends CloseableFrame {
public ActionExample1() {
super("Handling Events in Component");
setLayout(new FlowLayout());
setFont(new Font("Serif", Font.BOLD, 18));
add(new SetSizeButton(300, 200));
add(new SetSizeButton(400, 300));
add(new SetSizeButton(500, 400));
setSize(400, 300);
setVisible(true);
}
public static void main(String[] args) {
new ActionExample1();
}
}
37
Very closely analogous to the first approach from the event-
handling lecture (separate classes for event handlers).

        36.

    Decentralized Event Processing:
Example (Continued)
import java.awt.*;
import java.awt.event.*;
public class SetSizeButton extends Button
implements ActionListener {
private int width, height;
public SetSizeButton(int width, int height) {
super("Resize to " + width + "x" + height);
this.width = width;
this.height = height;
addActionListener(this);
}
public void actionPerformed(ActionEvent event) {
Container parent = getParent();
parent.setSize(width, height);
parent.invalidate();
parent.validate();

  <li itemprop="text">

    Centralized Event Processing:
Example (Continued)
public void actionPerformed(ActionEvent event) {
if (event.getSource() == button1) {
updateLayout(300, 200);
} else if (event.getSource() == button2) {
updateLayout(400, 300);
} else if (event.getSource() == button3) {
updateLayout(500, 400);
}
}
private void updateLayout(int width, int height) {
setSize(width, height);
invalidate();
validate();
}
public static void main(String[] args) {
new ActionExample2();
}
}41

    Semi-Centralized Event
Processing: Example (Cont)
private void updateLayout(int width, int height) {
setSize(width, height);
invalidate();
validate();
}
private class ResizeHandler implements ActionListener {
private int width, height;
public ResizeHandler(int width, int height) {
this.width= width;
this.height = height;
}
public void actionPerformed(ActionEvent event) {
updateLayout(width, height);
}
}
public static void main(String[] args) {
new ActionExample3();
}
}

handling lecture (inner classes for event handlers).

    Buttons
&#x2022; Constructors
&#x2013; Button()
Button(String buttonLabel)
&#x2022; The button size (preferred size) is based on the height and
width of the label in the current font, plus some extra
space determined by the OS
&#x2022; Useful Methods
&#x2013; getLabel/setLabel
&#x2022; Retrieves or sets the current label
&#x2022; If the button is already displayed, setting the label does not
automatically reorganize its Container
&#x2013; The containing window should be invalidated and validated to force
a fresh layout
someButton.setLabel("A New Label");
someButton.getParent().invalidate();
someButton.getParent().validate();

b1.addActionListener(listener);

    Checkboxes
&#x2022; Constructors
&#x2013; These three constructors apply to checkboxes that operate
independently of each other (i.e., not radio buttons)
&#x2013; Checkbox()
&#x2022; Creates an initially unchecked checkbox with no label
&#x2013; Checkbox(String checkboxLabel)
&#x2022; Creates a checkbox (initially unchecked) with the specified
label; see setState for changing it
&#x2013; Checkbox(String checkboxLabel, boolean state)
&#x2022; Creates a checkbox with the specified label
&#x2013; The initial state is determined by the boolean value provided
&#x2013; A value of true means it is checked
49

  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-48-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 48 image" target="_blank">
        48.
      </a>
    Checkbox, Example
public class Checkboxes extends CloseableFrame {
public Checkboxes() {
super("Checkboxes");
setFont(new Font("SansSerif", Font.BOLD, 18));
setLayout(new GridLayout(0, 2));
Checkbox box;
for(int i=0; i&lt;12; i++) {
box = new Checkbox("Checkbox " + i);
if (i%2 == 0) {
box.setState(true);
}
add(box);
}
pack();
setVisible(true);
}
}

    Other Checkbox Methods
&#x2022; getState/setState
&#x2013; Retrieves or sets the state of the checkbox: checked (true)
or unchecked (false)
&#x2022; getLabel/setLabel
&#x2013; Retrieves or sets the label of the checkbox
&#x2013; After changing the label invalidate and validate the
window to force a new layout
someCheckbox.setLabel("A New Label");
someCheckbox.getParent().invalidate();
someCheckbox.getParent().validate();
&#x2022; addItemListener/removeItemListener
&#x2013; Add or remove an ItemListener to process
ItemEvents in itemStateChanged
&#x2022; processItemEvent(ItemEvent event)
&#x2013; Low-level event handling

        50.
      </a>
    Handling Checkbox Events
&#x2022; Attach an ItemListener
&#x2013; Add it with addItemListener and process the ItemEvent in
itemStateChanged
public void itemStateChanged(ItemEvent event) {
...
}
&#x2022; The ItemEvent class has a getItem method which returns
the item just selected or deselected
&#x2022; The return value of getItem is an Object so you should
cast it to a String before using it
&#x2022; Ignore the event
&#x2013; With checkboxes, it is relatively common to ignore the
select/deselect event when it occurs
&#x2013; Instead, you look up the state (checked/unchecked) of the
checkbox later using the getState method of Checkbox
when you are ready to take some other sort of action52
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-51-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 51 image" target="_blank">
        51.
      </a>
    Checkbox Groups
(Radio Buttons)
&#x2022; CheckboxGroup Constructors
&#x2013; CheckboxGroup()
&#x2022; Creates a non-graphical object used as a &#x201C;tag&#x201D; to group
checkboxes logically together
&#x2022; Checkboxes with the same tag will look and act like radio
buttons
&#x2022; Only one checkbox associated with a particular tag can be
selected at any given time
&#x2022; Checkbox Constructors
&#x2013; Checkbox(String label, CheckboxGroup group,
boolean state)
&#x2022; Creates a radio button associated with the specified group,
with the given label and initial state
&#x2022; If you specify an initial state of true for more than one
Checkbox in a group, the last one will be shown selected
53
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-52-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 52 image" target="_blank">
        52.
      </a>
    CheckboxGroup: Example
import java.applet.Applet;
import java.awt.*;
public class CheckboxGroups extends Applet {
public void init() {
setLayout(new GridLayout(4, 2));
setBackground(Color.LIGHT_GRAY);
setFont(new Font("Serif", Font.BOLD, 16));
add(new Label("Flavor", Label.CENTER));
add(new Label("Toppings", Label.CENTER));
CheckboxGroup flavorGroup = new CheckboxGroup();
add(new Checkbox("Vanilla", flavorGroup, true));
add(new Checkbox("Colored Sprinkles"));
add(new Checkbox("Chocolate", flavorGroup, false));
add(new Checkbox("Cashews"));
add(new Checkbox("Strawberry", flavorGroup, false));
add(new Checkbox("Kiwi"));
}
}

    Other Methods for Radio

&#x2022; CheckboxGroup

        55.

    List Boxes
&#x2022; Constructors
&#x2013; List(int rows, boolean multiSelectable)
&#x2022; Creates a listbox with the specified number of visible rows (not
items)
&#x2022; Depending on the number of item in the list (addItem or add), a
scrollbar is automatically created
&#x2022; The second argument determines if the List is multiselectable
&#x2022; The preferred width is set to a platform-dependent value, and is
typically not directly related to the width of the widest entry
&#x2013; List()
&#x2022; Creates a single-selectable list box with a platform-dependent
number of rows and a platform-dependent width
&#x2013; List(int rows)
&#x2022; Creates a single-selectable list box with the specified number of
rows and a platform-dependent width
57
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-56-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 56 image" target="_blank">
        56.
      </a>
    List Boxes: Example
import java.awt.*;
public class Lists extends CloseableFrame {
public Lists() {
super("Lists");
setLayout(new FlowLayout());
setBackground(Color.LIGHT_GRAY);
setFont(new Font("SansSerif", Font.BOLD, 18));
List list1 = new List(3, false);
list1.add("Vanilla");
list1.add("Chocolate");
list1.add("Strawberry");
add(list1);
List list2 = new List(3, true);
list2.add("Colored Sprinkles");
list2.add("Cashews");
list2.add("Kiwi");
add(list2);
pack();
setVisible(true);
58
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-57-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 57 image" target="_blank">
        57.
      </a>
    List Boxes: Result
59
A list can be single-selectable or multi-selectable
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-58-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 58 image" target="_blank">
        58.
      </a>
    Other List Methods
&#x2022; add
&#x2013; Add an item at the end or specified position in the list box
&#x2013; All items at that index or later get moved down
&#x2022; isMultipleMode
&#x2013; Determines if the list is multiple selectable (true) or single
selectable (false)
&#x2022; remove/removeAll
&#x2013; Remove an item or all items from the list
&#x2022; getSelectedIndex
&#x2013; For a single-selectable list, this returns the index of the selected item
&#x2013; Returns &#x2013;1 if nothing is selected or if the list permits multiple
selections
&#x2022; getSelectedIndexes
&#x2013; Returns an array of the indexes of all selected items
&#x2022; Works for single- or multi-selectable lists
&#x2022; If no items are selected, a zero-length (but non-null) array is
returned60
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-59-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 59 image" target="_blank">
        59.
      </a>
    Other List Methods (Continued)
&#x2022; getSelectedItem
&#x2013; For a single-selectable list, this returns the label of the selected item
&#x2013; Returns null if nothing is selected or if the list permits multiple
selections
&#x2022; getSelectedItems
&#x2013; Returns an array of all selected items
&#x2013; Works for single- or multi-selectable lists
&#x2022; If no items are selected, a zero-length (but non-null) array is
returned
&#x2022; select
&#x2013; Programmatically selects the item in the list
&#x2013; If the list does not permit multiple selections, then the previously
selected item, if any, is also deselected
61
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-60-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 60 image" target="_blank">
        60.
      </a>
    Handling List Events
&#x2022; addItemListener/removeItemListener
&#x2013; ItemEvents are generated whenever an item is selected or
deselected (single-click)
&#x2013; Handle ItemEvents in itemStateChanged
&#x2022; addActionListener/removeActionListener
&#x2013; ActionEvents are generated whenever an item is double-
clicked or RETURN (ENTER) is pressed while selected
&#x2013; Handle ActionEvents in actionPerformed
62
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-61-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 61 image" target="_blank">
        61.
      </a>
    Other GUI Controls
&#x2022; Choice Lists (Combo Boxes)
&#x2022; Textfields
63
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-62-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 62 image" target="_blank">
        62.
      </a>
    Other GUI Controls (Continued)
&#x2022; Text Areas
&#x2022; Labels
64
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-63-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 63 image" target="_blank">
        63.
      </a>
    Summary
&#x2022; Native components behind the scenes
&#x2013; So, all windows and graphical components are rectangular and
opaque, and take look-and-feel of underlying OS.
&#x2022; Windows
&#x2013; Canvas: drawing area or custom component
&#x2013; Panel: grouping other components
&#x2013; Frame: popup window
&#x2022; GUI Controls
&#x2013; Button: handle events with ActionListener
&#x2013; Checkbox, radio button: handle events with ItemListener
&#x2013; List box: handle single click with ItemListener,
double click with ActionListener
&#x2013; To quickly determine the event handlers for a component,
simply look at the online API
&#x2022; addXxxListener methods are at the top
65
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/09-awt-components-120913162944-phpapp01/95/java-7-and-java-8-programming-tutorial-awt-components-simple-guis-64-638.jpg?cb=1406283677" title="View slide 64 image" target="_blank">
        64.
      </a>
